Local News

Wang Jingwei's Resignation Is Firm 115

Huang Shaoxiong Came to Shanghai Yesterday Morning to Persuade Him, But Did Not Get to See Him

Wang Jingwei, the President of the Executive Yuan, arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday and, on the afternoon of that day at 4:00 PM, telegraphed five letters of resignation and moved to a new residence in western Shanghai, refusing to see guests. Details of yesterday are recorded as follows:

▲Ministers of Various Yuan Jointly Persuade Him to Stay After receiving Wang's resignation telegram at 4:30 PM the day before yesterday in Nanjing, the ministers of the central government's various Yuan immediately convened an emergency meeting to discuss countermeasures. It was decided to send Minister of Interior Huang Shaoxiong, together with Vice Minister of Railways Zeng Zhongming, to Shanghai to persuade him to stay on behalf of the central government. Meanwhile, the ministers of the central government's various Yuan remaining in Nanjing jointly sent a letter to Wang. The content of the letter requested that Wang make an effort to overcome difficulties in this time of national crisis, and stated that if there were changes in the central government at this critical juncture, the overall situation would be worrying. They requested that he withdraw his resignation and return to Nanjing immediately to face the national crisis together. The letter was signed by Yu Youren, President of the Control Yuan; Shao Yuanchong, President of the Legislative Yuan; Huang Shaoxiong, Minister of Interior and concurrently Minister of Communications; Luo Wengan, Minister of Foreign Affairs and concurrently Minister of Judicial Administration; Gu Mengyu, Minister of Railways, and others. That evening, a special envoy was dispatched to send the original letter to Shanghai, requesting that Ju Zheng, President of the Judicial Yuan, Chen Gongbo, Minister of Industry, and Zhu Jiahua, Minister of Education, who were in Shanghai, add their signatures. Finally, it was sent to Song Ziwen, Minister of Finance, for him to add his signature, and was sent to Wang's residence on Rue de la Poste at around 10:00 AM yesterday, and then forwarded to Wang.

▲Huang Shaoxiong Came to Shanghai to Persuade Wang Huang Shaoxiong, Minister of Interior and concurrently Minister of Communications, flew to Shanghai the day before yesterday under orders to persuade Wang to stay. Zeng Zhongming, Vice Minister of Railways and Wang's confidant, also came to Shanghai. The two took a China National Aviation Corporation plane from Nanjing at 4:30 PM and arrived at Longhua Airport at around 6:00 PM the day before yesterday. Huang resided at Room 217 of the Cangzhou Hotel, while Zeng Zhongming visited Wang. Wang had originally scheduled to meet Huang at his residence at 8:00 AM yesterday, but when Huang visited, Wang had not yet returned to his residence, so they did not meet. According to Vice Minister of Railways Zeng Zhongming, who spoke to the Hua Dong News Agency reporter yesterday afternoon, Minister Huang did not have the opportunity to meet Mr. Wang today. If there is an opportunity this afternoon or tomorrow morning, they should be able to discuss everything in person. Minister Huang's visit is solely to persuade Mr. Wang to stay, and there are no other tasks, he said.

▲Zeng Visited Song Yesterday Evening and Returned to Nanjing Vice Minister of Railways Zeng Zhongming visited Wang the night before last after flying from Nanjing to Shanghai. At 8:10 AM yesterday, Zeng, on Wang's orders, went to Song's residence on Qiqi Road to meet with Song Ziwen, Vice President of the Executive Yuan and concurrently Minister of Finance. After talking for only five minutes, he hurriedly left. When Zeng left Song's residence, he told the Hua Dong News Agency reporter that the purpose of his visit to Song was to explain Wang's reasons for resigning and to ask Song to return to Nanjing immediately and, in his position as Vice President, concurrently take over the duties of President, so that the central government's affairs would not be suspended as a result. However, Song's attitude was still very humble, and there was no definite date for his return to Nanjing, he said. Zeng went to Nanjing last night.

▲Zeng Talks About the Reasons for Wang's Resignation A reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency met Zeng Zhongming at Wang's residence at 10:45 AM yesterday. According to him, Mr. Wang's resignation this time is due to his deep disapproval of Zhang Xueliang, Director of the Peiping Pacification Headquarters, using the name of resistance to gather money. Now that Wang is the President of the Executive Yuan, he could have ordered his dismissal, but for the sake of the overall situation, after repeated consideration, he had no choice but to resign to take responsibility, and at the same time urge Zhang to realize his mistake. It is a proactive resignation, not a passive one. If the central government approves his resignation, then Mr. Wang is willing to take on party affairs work and can return to Nanjing within days. I visited Minister Song today purely to report the important reasons for President Wang's resignation. Minister of Interior and concurrently Minister of Communications Huang Shaoxiong has arrived in Shanghai, but has not yet met with Wang. He will probably meet Wang this afternoon. Huang is here to represent the central government in persuading Wang to return to Nanjing, but Wang's attitude towards resigning is firm, and there is no question of persuading him to stay. Wang's departure or stay is entirely for the public good, and not for ordinary reasons. As for the rumors that Wang telegraphed Zhang Xueliang to resign together and apologize to the people of the country, containing a sense of revenge, it is really not worth the laughter of knowledgeable people. In fact, there is no personal prejudice. The various departments have not yet made any indication, he said.

▲Wang Will Not Go Anywhere Else in Shanghai After submitting his resignation to the central government, Wang moved to a new residence on Rue Jules Joffre in western Shanghai, closed his door and rested quietly, refusing to see all guests. As for Wang's slight illness, he has fully recovered. According to Tang Youren, who spoke to the Central News Agency reporter, all kinds of rumors such as Wang leaving Shanghai to go elsewhere are untrue. Wang is currently staying in Shanghai to recuperate and will not go anywhere else. If the National Government approves Wang's resignation, he will return to Nanjing immediately to continue serving the party and the country, he said.

▲Minister of Finance Song Temporarily Suspends Going to Nanjing According to the Central News Agency, after learning of Wang's resignation and receiving a telegram from Nanjing urging him to go to Nanjing immediately to act as President of the Executive Yuan, Minister of Finance Song Ziwen decided the night before last to take a plane back to Nanjing at 6:00 AM yesterday. The plane that Song took to Shanghai the day before last was already prepared for departure at Hongqiao Airport. It was temporarily suspended due to some matter. The Central News Agency reporter met Song at the office of Zhang Shouyong, an advisor to the Ministry of Finance, yesterday. According to him, regarding the issue of President Wang's resignation, I have expressed my hope that Wang will still make an effort to take on the difficult task. As for the date of return to Nanjing, it is undecided, he said. It is also learned that Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Minister of Education Zhu Jiahua, and Vice President of the Academia Sinica Yang Xingfo visited Song at around 4:00 PM yesterday to discuss the issue of persuading President Wang to withdraw his resignation. According to Mayor Wu, there have been considerable results. Minister Song visited Zhang Shouyong at around 5:00 PM yesterday to discuss financial issues, and left after about fifteen minutes. According to Zhang, when sending Song to board the car, Song's visit was of a friendly nature, and the financial issues of the government were also mentioned. Although I have resigned from the position of Vice Minister of Finance, I will still assist Song in everything out of friendship, he said. It was also reported that Minister of Finance Song Ziwen sent a letter to President of the Executive Yuan Wang Jingwei yesterday morning, requesting a scheduled date to discuss everything. In the afternoon, Wang replied and Zeng Zhongming took it to Song's residence. According to Zeng, President Wang's resignation is very firm, but it is definitely not passive. Minister of Interior Huang Shaoxiong has not yet met with Minister Song after arriving in Shanghai. They are scheduled to visit each other tomorrow (today), he said.

▲Wang's Wife, Chen Bijun, Arrives in Shanghai According to Tang Youren, Secretary-General of the Central Political Conference, who spoke to the Central News Agency reporter, Wang's wife, Chen Bijun, arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning from Jiujiang Lushan on a China National Aviation Corporation plane. After arriving in Shanghai, Wang's wife returned to her private residence on Rue de la Poste. After learning that Wang had moved to a new residence, she immediately took a car to the new residence to express her condolences.

▲Telegrams of Condolences and Persuasion Arrive From Various Places Wang's residence in Shanghai received eighteen telegrams of condolences and persuasion yesterday from Chairman Chiang of the Military Affairs Commission and various ministries and commissions in Nanjing. Kong Xiangxi, special envoy to Europe to investigate industry, and Minister of Education Zhu Jiahua also sent lengthy letters to Wang to comfort and persuade him yesterday. The General Federation of Shanghai North Business Circles in this city sent representatives Xing Min, Qiu Liangyu, and Cao Youguang to visit Wang yesterday with a letter. Because Wang was not at his residence, the secretary met them on his behalf. The original letter stated, "President Jingwei, greetings. According to reports, your Excellency suddenly has the intention of retiring. We, the humble people, are shocked and terrified. At this time of national crisis, we rely on unity from top to bottom to resist foreign aggression together. Your Excellency leads from the front, and the people can follow from behind. If there are illegal soldiers who dare to coerce, then not only will the cessation of civil war be implemented, but the people will also pledge to be a backing. Our association represents all the people in Shanghai North, earnestly pleading to stay on, do not give rise to the idea of retreat, and please make an effort to overcome difficulties, strive to fight, firmly adhere to the original intention, and comfort the expectations of the people. Furthermore, our association plans to take advantage of your Excellency's visit to Shanghai, a once-in-a-lifetime opportunity, to request an inspection of the disaster area, so as to know the suffering of the locality. Therefore, we have appointed Qiu Liangyu, Xing Min, and Cao Youguang to visit Your Excellency. We respectfully hope that you will deign to grant an audience, present our suffering, and provide assistance. On behalf of the disaster victims of Shanghai North, we thank you deeply. We respectfully wish you good health. Respectfully, The General Federation of Shanghai North Business Circles." Furthermore, the General Labor Union of this city sent a letter to Wang Jingwei yesterday, saying, "Greetings to Mr. Jingwei. Yesterday, we read in the newspaper that, because the central government's finances are exhausted and difficult to maintain, and recently due to the Rehe incident, you feel more and more difficult, you suddenly resigned from the position of President of the Executive Yuan. After hearing this, we are inexplicably horrified. Since you took on the difficult task of presiding over the central government, you have worked diligently day and night and achieved great results. Now that the strong enemy is approaching and the Red Terror is rampant, internal and external troubles are intertwined, the people of the country are looking forward to you breaking through the difficulties, stabilizing the foundation of the country, and rescuing the people from water and fire. Unexpectedly, you suddenly announced your retirement, causing the central government to be without a responsible person, and the overall situation is becoming more and more chaotic. Thinking of the future, we cannot help but shudder. After repeated consideration, our association can only plead with you to prioritize national affairs, withdraw your resignation, return to Nanjing to resume your post, continue your efforts with perseverance and determination, and comfort the people's eager expectations. We earnestly state our words and hope that you will consider and accept them."

Industry and Commerce Respond to Wang's Telegram 116

▲Criticize Zhang Xueliang One After Another

▲The National General Chamber of Commerce Sends a Telegram to the Public The National General Chamber of Commerce telegraphed Zhang Xueliang, Director of the Peiping Pacification Headquarters, yesterday, asking him to rise up and resist to recover the lost territories of the Northeast. The original telegram stated, "Greetings to Director Zhang Hanqing of the Peiping Pacification Headquarters. We read in today's newspaper that President Wang sent your Excellency a telegram. We imagine that your Excellency will either advance to kill the enemy or retreat and give way to the worthy, and will have made a decision early. It is not necessary to repeat ourselves. However, what is called China is the China of the Chinese people. Sitting and watching the strong enemy invade without resisting, and being unable to recover the lost territories, the people of the country cry bitterly, and there is something that cannot be stopped in words. Since the Japanese bandits attacked Shenyang on September 18 last year, your Excellency was living leisurely in Peiping and Tianjin, and lightly ordered the front-line generals not to resist, and led the troops of the country to defend the territory without fighting and retreat. This is mistake number one. Since the fall of Shenyang, the enemy's power has become more rampant. Ma Zhanshan and others rose up to raise troops in Heihe, vowing to fight Japan to the death. At that time, if your Excellency led troops to advance together, attacking from both east and west, it would not be difficult to drive back the strong enemy in one go. Your Excellency did not plan this, and sat and watched the enemy take Jilin and Heilongjiang in the east and invade Jinzhou and Yu in the west, occupying Manchuria and forming a puppet state, thus starting the intention to attack Shanghai. This is mistake number two. The Nineteenth Route Army and the Fifth Route Army fought against the Japanese bandits in Shanghai for thirty-four days. The Japanese bandits repeatedly mobilized large armies and attacked with all their strength. At that time, if your Excellency hurriedly led troops to drive out the enemy from the pass, making it impossible for the enemy to take care of both ends, the enemy would surely be defeated on both routes. It would not only recover the lost territories of the Northeast, but also the anti-Japanese troops in Shanghai would not have been oppressed and retreated due to the enemy's leisurely reinforcements. Your Excellency still did not plan this. This is mistake number three. After the Battle of Shanghai, the agreement was signed, and the Northeast Volunteer Army rose up to kill the enemy. With untrained volunteer soldiers, knowing that they were no match, but driven by patriotism, everyone died, attacking Jinzhou and Liaoning in the morning, and attacking Shenyang and Yingkou at night, fighting to the death with the strong enemy. At that time, if your Excellency advanced and led them, and used the large army as a backing, the strong enemy, no matter how strong, would still not be enough to drive out. But your Excellency has paid no attention to it, like the people of Qin watching Yue. This is mistake number four. Now, in order to cover up the puppet state's plan, the enemy is advancing to Rehe and peeping at Peiping and Tianjin. The central government has repeatedly ordered resistance, and cannot lose another inch of land. But your Excellency has not sent troops, but first asked for huge sums of money. Our association does not dare to hastily say that your Excellency is using the name of resistance to gather money, knowing that the central government's finances are exhausted, and deliberately making things difficult. We cannot help but suspect that you are using it as an excuse to demand money. Now the enemy is deep, and the matter is urgent. We do not have time to interrogate the past. For the sake of the country and for your own sake, your Excellency should quickly reorganize the army, consolidate the defenses of Rehe, and recover the Northeast to redeem your previous sins. If you cannot, then please resign according to President Wang's telegram to apologize to the people of the country. Otherwise, you will miss the opportunity for military action. The national law may be able to forgive your Excellency, but the people of the country cannot forgive your Excellency. The difference between a sage and a thief is in one thought. What to do and where to go, only your Excellency can choose. The national crisis is pressing, and the words are not taboo. We humbly await your orders. Respectfully, The National General Chamber of Commerce."

▲Various Labor Unions Send Telegrams to Yu The Shanghai Publishing Industry Labor Union Organizing Committee and other groups jointly telegraphed the central government yesterday, saying, "Most urgent, greetings to the Central Party Headquarters and the National Government in Nanjing. Upon reading President Wang's telegram, we learned that Zhang Xueliang has consistently adhered to the policy of non-resistance, and is unwilling to send troops to resist Japan. Instead, he is using economic issues to blackmail the central government, so he resigned in anger to apologize to Zhang alone, and also asked Zhang to resign to apologize to the 400 million people of the country. President Wang's words are impassioned and tragic, deeply winning the hearts of our people. Zhang Xueliang, entrusted with the heavy responsibility of the government and enjoying the superior support of the people, held the important position of the Northeast border defense commander, but he actually adhered to the policy of non-resistance, allowing Shenyang and other important towns to be occupied by the Japanese. When defending Jinzhou, the matter could still be planned but was not done. Without firing a single bullet, he retreated entirely into the pass. Now that the violent sun is invading Rehe and peeping at Peiping and Tianjin, Zhang Xueliang is still numb as before, making no preparations at all, and is using the name of raising funds to blackmail the central government, still leisurely thinking that he is pleased with himself. This kind of military man who has lost territory and humiliated the country should have been executed, how can we let him leisurely enjoy himself, let him take his course, losing control of one person and ruining the survival of the country and nation? Now that the fire is burning our eyebrows, how can we discuss it in advance? We urge the central government to immediately issue a resolute order to dismiss Zhang Xueliang from his post and investigate him, and to immediately order the Military Affairs Commission to mobilize the entire country, quickly send troops to the Northeast, recover the lost territories, and implement President Wang's anti-Japanese proposal. Then our people of the entire country will surely be the backing of the government. We await your order with the utmost urgency. The Shanghai Publishing Industry Labor Union Organizing Committee, Seamen's Union, Dockworkers' Union, Shanghai East District Yarn Factory Federation, etc."

▲The Transportation Industry Association and Others Issue a Declaration The Shanghai Transportation and Customs Declaration Association, the Commercial Gang Association, and other public groups issued a declaration yesterday, saying, "Since the Shenyang Incident, those in our country who have huge armies have adhered to the policy of non-resistance, sitting idly by and watching the Northeast be lost without regret. Temporary Martial Law Yesterday 117

▲The Night Remained Peaceful as Usual

The Municipal Public Security Bureau and the Concession Police Department received secret reports a few days ago that the communists would take action on August 7 (yesterday). After receiving the report, the two authorities announced martial law in various places yesterday, stepping up precautions to avoid unexpected events. The details are recorded as follows:

▲North Railway Station The Municipal Public Security Bureau received a report a few days ago that hundreds of communists would gather at the North Railway Station on the morning of August 7 to hold a meeting, and would have various unruly actions, attempting to disturb local public security. After receiving the report, the Municipal Public Security Bureau immediately ordered increased precautions. From 8:00 AM yesterday, the Fifth District General Office dispatched a full class of secret agents to station themselves around the North Railway Station to provide tight security. The security team also dispatched a security police squad and a red security vehicle to be stationed at the North Station, responsible for security. He Yiming, the district chief of the Fifth District, and Huang Ming, the director of the security regiment, also went to the station to supervise and inspect. At the same time, the Concession Police Department also dispatched a large number of detectives to station themselves along the boundary road, providing strict security. At the corner of North Henan Road, a security vehicle was parked in advance, paying close attention to pedestrians. However, from 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM, nothing happened. In the afternoon, the detectives were withdrawn and replaced by a large police team to patrol back and forth.

▲Yangshupu The Concession Police Department received a secret report a few days ago that on the morning of August 7, the communists would take advantage of the Sunday holiday to promote the Rehe Incident and the anti-Japanese movement to workers in various factories in Yangshupu, attempting to incite strikes, marches, and demonstrations. The Yangshupu Police Department dispatched more than a hundred Chinese and Western detectives to various districts from 8:00 AM yesterday to provide strict security to prevent any unexpected gatherings. All gatherings were prohibited. In places such as Pingliang Road, Yulin Road, Liaoyang Road, and Lan Road, there were large numbers of detectives stationed, paying particular attention to those who looked like workers. From morning to dusk, security was maintained throughout, so fortunately no unexpected incidents occurred.

▲French Concession The French Municipal Police Department specially dispatched many detectives yesterday morning (the 7th), all armed, to guard the bridges in the area of Zhaojiabang and Xujiahui, providing temporary security, and closed the iron gates in various places, providing strict precautions. However, no accidents occurred until the evening, so the detectives were withdrawn and the original state was restored.

Cotton Yarn Tax Rate Issues 120

Tracing back, our nation was founded on agriculture, with silk and hemp being major elements. Since the rise of the textile industry, cotton planting and mechanical weaving have become important real industries. However, up to today, they still cannot be fully developed. Is it not due to poor human planning, but also the nation's failure to fully promote them? Cotton planting belongs to agriculture, and textile manufacturing belongs to machinery. Both are specialized technologies. Today's advocates of new agricultural science and engineers proficient in textiles are constantly striving for excellence. However, the smooth flow of goods is crucial, especially concerning taxation. Now, at a time when we are initiating the promotion of domestic goods, society is paying closer attention to the textile industry. This newspaper has specifically interviewed a certain gentleman in the textile industry, first discussing the issue of tariffs, so that the world knows the urgent need to promote domestic goods. Moreover, promoting domestic goods especially depends on the nation establishing protective policies as a pioneer. The following is the gentleman's statement:

China's textile industry began in the late Qing Dynasty, initiated by Li Wenzhong. The China Merchants Textile New Bureau was his first creation, which is today's Shanghai Hengfeng Yarn Factory. At that time, the nation advocated mechanical manufacturing, and the tariffs on machine-made foreign goods were specifically lower than other types of goods, to resist imported products. The export tax on cotton yarn was 7 mace (關平七錢) per dan (担), equivalent to 8 mace (銀八錢) based on the current 98 standard silver dollar (規元). Each dan is 320 catties (斤), so the tax was 2 taels (關平二兩) and 2.4 mace (二錢四分), equivalent to 2 taels (規元二兩) and 5.6 mace (五錢六分) in standard silver dollars. This has been in place for over twenty years without increase. However, after the European War, the Washington Conference passed the addition of surtaxes for China. The original intention of adding surtaxes was to increase import taxes, so that domestic industries could gain more protection, and not to add them to domestic products. However, at that time, in 1923, Sun Chuanfang governed Jiangsu, and the increased tariffs were also applied to domestic goods. Thus, the original cotton yarn tax of 2 taels (二兩) and 5.6 mace (五錢六分) per bale was increased to 3 taels (三兩) and 8.4 mace (八錢四分).

In 1927, the National Government was established, with many military expenditures and insufficient national funds. By 1930, there were renewed discussions about increasing the yarn tax. However, due to the large number of Japanese-owned yarn factories in the country, implementing the tax increase required prior negotiation with them. Therefore, people were sent to negotiate, proposing 6 yuan (元) per dan, equivalent to 18 yuan (元) per bale. From June to November, there were back-and-forth rejections. At that time, Chinese-owned yarn factories, upon hearing the news, also rose up in opposition and presented the advantages and disadvantages to the Legislative Yuan. As a result, a special tax was implemented (now merged into the consolidated tax). For coarse yarn of 23 counts and below, the tax was 2 taels (挩銀二元) and 7.5 mace (七角五分) per dan, equivalent to 8 yuan (八元) and 5.8 mace (五角八分) or 6 taels (規元六兩) and 2.5 mace (二錢五分) in standard silver dollars per 320-catty bale. For fine yarn above 23 counts, the tax was 3 taels (稅銀三元) and 7.5 mace (七角五分) per dan, equivalent to 11 yuan (十一元) and 6.3 mace (六角三分) or 8 taels (規元八兩) and 3 mace (三錢) in standard silver dollars per bale. The increase was more than double.

Moreover, looking back before the implementation of the special tax, when the tariff increased from 2 taels (二兩) and 5.6 mace (五錢六分) to 3 taels (三兩) and 8.4 mace (八錢四分), the collected tax was a tariff. Sales within the province and nearby rural areas initially did not require tariffs, except for the reed mat fee of 1-2 yuan per bale. When the new system was implemented, it was called a consolidated tax, and all cotton yarn leaving the factory was taxed. Even sales within the province and nearby rural areas were subject to the same tax rate. Factories in the interior (such as Nantong and Wuxi), which previously sold part of their products nearby and did not bear this tax, now uniformly bear it, making business even more difficult to develop.

The raw material for cotton yarn manufacturing is cotton. The quality of cotton in our country is relatively inferior, so imported cotton must be used. The import tax on cotton has always been 1 tael (銀一兩) and 2 mace (二錢) per dan. Since the tariff began to be levied in gold units, the tax rate has risen to 3 taels (銀三兩). Each bale of cotton yarn requires more than 300 catties (斤) of cotton. Therefore, the factory's output of cotton yarn, in addition to paying a tax rate of 6 taels (六兩) and 2.5 mace (二錢五分) or 8 taels (八兩) and 3 mace (三錢) per bale, must also bear the import tax on more than 300 catties (斤) of raw materials, totaling 10 taels (十兩) and 7-8 mace (七八錢). This is something unheard of in other countries. Comparing it to the yarn tax in Japan, their domestic sales of yarn made from imported cotton, without exporting it, are taxed 17-18 taels (十七八兩) less per bale than our domestic factories, saving on tariffs and imported cotton. Moreover, their exports of finished yarn are also taxed 10 taels (十兩) and 7-8 mace (七八錢) less per bale for the imported cotton. As for Chinese-produced cotton, although not abundant or of the highest quality, it is still quite usable. However, the difficulty of procurement and local demands constantly make merchants hesitant. For example, in the Laohekou area of central Hubei two years ago, over 400,000 dan of fine cotton were produced, priced at only 20 yuan (元) per dan, which was not expensive. Merchants went to procure it, but the upstream area of Laohekou was the location of bandit troops, and the downstream route to Shashi was occupied by provincial troops. The merchants negotiated with the bandit troops, who demanded 4 yuan (元) per dan for passage. They negotiated with the provincial troops, whose headquarters demanded 6 yuan (元) per dan for escort. However, even after paying 6 yuan (元), the headquarters' orders still could not be enforced. The stationed troops demanded another 6 yuan (元) per dan to allow passage. The merchants had no choice but to pay. Thus, the cost of the purchased cotton, not including transportation, was burdened with 16 yuan (元) per dan, making it unbearable. No one dared to try again. Northern railways' transportation rights were mostly controlled by stationed troops, who would not transport goods without additional car fees. Japanese merchants buying cotton in Jinan, due to their special influence on the Jiaoji Railway, could transport goods at any time by paying only the standard freight fee, with no other demands. Therefore, Chinese factories were forced to buy domestic cotton from Japanese merchants, which is regrettable. As a result, farmers who plant cotton have almost no one to sell to, making them even more distressed. Considering imported cotton, in the most recent cotton accounting year, from July of the twelfth year of the Republic to June of this year, the total imports of American cotton were about 1 million bales, equivalent to more than 3.7 million dan, valued at over 110 million taels (兩) in standard silver dollars. This does not include Indian cotton, which is also a significant amount. Considering China as an agricultural country, and that cotton, a crucial agricultural product, depends so heavily on foreigners, with so much money flowing out, how can the nation sustain itself?

Regarding domestic cotton planting, since the Chinese Yarn Factory Association requested Southeast University to experiment with improved cotton seeds in the second year of the Republic, nearly twenty years have passed, and over 100,000 yuan (元) has been spent. However, the results have not been very common, due to two reasons. First, it is difficult to distribute high-quality seeds to various provinces and villages. Second, the most suitable provinces and villages for cotton planting are the northern provinces of Shanxi, Henan, Shaanxi, and Shandong. However, the farmers in those areas find the profits from planting opium far greater than from planting cotton. The sale of cotton is not always easy, and farmers do not have the ability to store it for long periods. Opium, on the other hand, can be sold immediately after harvesting, yielding higher profits.

Cotton production in the Northwest is also strong, with Xinjiang's cotton being especially good. However, due to inconvenient transportation and the time required for shipping, it cannot circulate smoothly within the country. Some factories in Tianjin and Shanghai have tried buying Xinjiang cotton, mostly in small packages of 14 pounds each, sent by post, with postage of over one yuan per package. Those who plan for the nation should truly understand that the land yields benefits.

Since the September 18th Incident, Japanese goods have been subject to boycotts, leading to sluggish sales of Japanese cotton. As a result, they compete by lowering prices. For every bale of Chinese yarn sold at 160 taels (兩), Japanese yarn sells for 140 taels (兩). When the price of Chinese yarn drops, the price of Japanese yarn drops accordingly, until Chinese yarn can no longer drop and can no longer be sold. This cannot be called dumping, but only disruption. The same is true for cotton cloth. For example, Chinese factory-made oil-dyed twill sells for 6 taels (六兩) and 2 mace (二錢) per bolt, while Japanese goods sell for 4 taels (四兩) and 8 mace (八錢). This is an extreme example of destructive capabilities, but it is still difficult for both sides to sell smoothly. However, due to economic and transportation factors, sales in the North have not decreased. As for the sales price related to the raw material cost, the average selling price of Chinese factory yarn is around 160 taels (兩) per bale, which is not high. However, due to the fluctuating market price, the difference is significant, reducing people's purchasing power and causing merchants to wait and see, resulting in sluggish sales. Therefore, it cannot be blamed on the high price of yarn. Around 160 taels (兩) is the lowest price in the past three years. Moreover, the raw material is imported foreign cotton, and the price of gold has more than doubled. Given these factors, the selling price is not exorbitant. Some say that the price of Chinese yarn has risen after the boycott of Japanese goods, but this is an overestimation.

Page 15

Fire Insurance Compensation Issues During the Shanghai War 122

▲ Tongtai Yong vs. Hequn Company

▲ Appeal Judgment: Tongtai Loses

▲ Danger Arising from Hostile Actions

▲ Not Within the Insurance Contract

After the cessation of the Sino-Japanese Shanghai War, among the lawsuits accepted by the First Special District Court, the outcome of two cases depended on this war. One is the dispute over the termination of the ship charter contract between Yuan'an Shipping Company and Shanghai Zhongwei Shipping Company, which is still under trial, because Zhongwei denied that the Shanghai War was a formal war and refused to terminate the contract, leading to the lawsuit. The outcome is still uncertain. The other is the case of Tongtai Yong, which was burned down by Japanese troops attacking Chinese troops on February 2nd. Its manager, Chen Lianghuai, wanted to force Hequn Business Company to compensate for the insured fire insurance money. Therefore, he deliberately made a statement against his conscience, saying that his store was not burned down due to military affairs. However, the store was located at 3263-3266 Seward Road, Hongkou, which was completely within the occupied area of the Japanese army. Therefore, at 5:00 AM on February 2nd, the store's employees had already fled. The building was shot by guns and cannons, causing a fire. Although the Chinese members of the Public Works Department fire brigade also drove to rescue it, they were not allowed by the Japanese army. All buildings and goods were burned to ashes, and the fire extinguished itself. The estimated loss reached 58,999 taels. The store had a total of 97,000 taels of fire insurance, of which 10,000 taels were insured by Hequn Business Company on behalf of the German company Selegi Yage Company. After being sued, Hequn hired Lawyer Shen Yuesheng to file a defense, exhaustively listing reasons why it should not be liable for compensation for the loss, especially emphasizing the provisions of Article 6 of the insurance contract. First Special Court Civil Division Judge Shen Hong repeatedly gathered evidence, summoned all witnesses, and held hearings, which have already concluded. The judgment was announced the day before yesterday, rejecting the plaintiff's lawsuit and the request for provisional execution, with the plaintiff bearing the litigation costs. The judgment has already been sent to the officers yesterday. If there is any dissatisfaction, an appeal may be filed with the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court within 20 days after delivery. The reasoning in the judgment is excerpted as follows:

In this case, the plaintiff claimed compensation from the defendant based on the insurance contract, while the defendant's defense can be divided into three points: (1) The plaintiff entered into the insurance contract with Selegi Yage Insurance Company, and the defendant is only an agent and is not liable according to the law. (2) Article 21 of the insurance contract states that the company's agent is not responsible for the company's litigation behavior or other investigative behavior, and the insured shall not seek to compensate for damages from the agent's own property. (3) The excluded risks in clause B of Article 6 of the insurance contract. The court found that the signatory on the insurance contract and the insurance receipt was the defendant Hequn Business Co., Ltd. Although there was also the imprinted German company Selegi Yage Insurance Company and the word "agent" in Western text under Hequn Business Co., Ltd., the envelope of the insurance contract given by the defendant to the plaintiff was labeled as the insurance department of Shanghai Hequn Business Co., Ltd., without the Chinese word "agent." It is inferred that the plaintiff at the time actually trusted Hequn Business Company as the insurer. The defendant cannot deny the inconsistency of the plaintiff's claim by claiming to be a nominal agent. Even if we concede a step, Selegi Yage Insurance Company is a foreign company and has not registered with our National Registration Bureau. According to Article 15 of the Implementation Law of the General Principles of the Civil Code, its actors should still bear joint and several liability. As for the section in Article 21 of the insurance contract, as mentioned above, its defense claim is also difficult to establish. However, clause B of Article 6 of the insurance contract states that dangers arising from acts of war, such as aggression and foreign hostile actions, are not within the scope of the insurance contract. Therefore, to resolve whether the defendant is liable for compensation, it is necessary to determine whether the above circumstances exist. According to the plaintiff's statement, the cause of the fire in the insured house was that the war was very dangerous at the time, there was no one in the store, and the details are not known now. Witness Pier Mulumutuchen stated that before Tongtai Yong caught fire, he heard gunshots at 4:00 AM and saw Japanese sailors below during the day. Witness Bolasi stated that when we went to put out the fire, we heard gunshots at the Wuchang Road intersection. Because there was danger ahead, the Japanese navy prevented us from moving forward, so we stopped. Witness Bai Ke stated that in February, Chinese people could not go to Hongkou Zhabei for insurance matters for various Chinese and foreign insurance companies, so foreigners went. I also went with a pass. Tongtai Yong's address was under the jurisdiction of the Japanese army. On February 2nd, I went to Tongtai Yong to inspect and saw a group of Japanese soldiers. I asked the Japanese officer how Tongtai Yong caught fire, and he said that at 5:00 AM, someone attacked them, and they retaliated. When the plaintiff's insured house was burned, that place was indeed occupied by the invading Japanese army, and there was danger arising from hostile actions, caused by foreign hostile actions. There is considerable evidence to prove this. According to clause B of Article 6 of the insurance contract, the plaintiff is unable to claim that the defendant is liable for compensation. Although the plaintiff submitted a reply letter from the headquarters of the 19th Route Army, stating that there was no organization of plainclothes teams during the military operations of our army, this can only prove that there was no plainclothes team at that time. That letter does not provide contrary evidence to the hostile actions of the Japanese army invading the area. Therefore, it cannot be used to overturn the above evidence. Furthermore, Hequn Business Co., Ltd. has been registered, and Miao Jinfathe and others are the company's executive directors. The defendant submitted the company's registration license, causing the plaintiff's agent to withdraw the lawsuit against Miao Jinfathe and others in court. However, it is inappropriate to subsequently declare in court that Miao and others are still the defendants. As for the request for a declaration of provisional execution, since the plaintiff's lawsuit cannot be considered justified, it should not be discussed. In conclusion, the plaintiff's lawsuit is unjustified. In accordance with Article 81 of the Civil Procedure Law, the judgment is rendered as stated in the main text.

Youth Association Accounting Clerk Murdered 123

▲ Gong Yanru was Diligent in His Work

▲ A Trip to Ming Yuan From Which He Did Not Return

▲ The Location in the Huangpu River Where the Body Was Discovered

▲ The Death Appears to Have Been Caused by Robbery

Gong Yanru, the accounting clerk of the Shanghai Youth Association, went out for a stroll on the evening of the 4th of this month and suddenly disappeared. His body was found in the Huangpu River the day before yesterday (the 6th). After examination, it was discovered that there was a knife wound on the left side of his neck, leaving no doubt that he was murdered. However, how he was killed is still unclear. The details are as follows:

▲ Gong Jun's Background Gong Jun was a native of Yueyang, Hunan, 42 years old. He used to work in business circles in Tianjin and Hankou. Last summer, he took the position of accounting clerk at the Youth Association. He was diligent in his work and got along well with his colleagues. On the evening of the 4th of this month, at 8:00 PM, after having dinner at home, he went to Ming Yuan Amusement Park. When he left, his demeanor was as usual. He even told his children that he would buy some candy to bring back.

▲ A Trip to Ming Yuan From Which He Did Not Return That evening, his colleague Mr. Yang and old friend Mr. Zhang were also at Ming Yuan to escape the heat. They both met him and had a pleasant conversation. Unexpectedly, Gong Jun did not return home that night, and there was still no news the next day. His family was extremely anxious and asked people to look for him everywhere. They also reported it to the police and the water police bureau.

▲ Discovery of the Body On the 6th of this month, a body was found in the Huangpu River near Lujiazui. It was retrieved by the Tongren Fuyuan Hall Lifesaving Bureau. His family went to identify it upon hearing the news. It was indeed Gong Jun's body. They immediately reported it to the Shanghai Local Court. Yesterday, the court sent a prosecutor to examine the body. It was discovered that there was a knife wound on the left side of his neck, confirming that he had been murdered. Lawyer Yao Xian, representing the family of the deceased, immediately claimed the body, prepared it for burial, and requested the court to strictly arrest the murderer and punish them according to the law.

▲ Speculation About the Murder According to the prosecutor's opinion, the knife wound did not appear to be fatal, and there was a lot of water in his abdomen, suggesting that he may not have been dead when he fell into the water. It is believed that he was stabbed and then pushed into the Huangpu River. According to his family, Gong Jun had more than 30 yuan in cash, a wristwatch, and a gold watch with him when he went out on the evening of the 4th. All of these are now missing. It is suspected that he was robbed and murdered by bandits. Gong Jun had a total of seven children, all of whom are dependent on him. This sudden misfortune is deeply regrettable.

Two Bandits Who Kidnapped a Female School Principal Executed by Firing Squad in Suzhou 124

Ding Xitian, Weng Desheng (also known as Wen Desheng), Ding Xibiao, and others, lake bandits involved in the case of colluding to hold weapons and blocking the small ferry from Suzhou to Dongting East Mountain to kidnap Fu Zhongde, the female principal of Zhongxiu Elementary School in Dongshan, fled to Shanghai after the incident and hid in Lujiawan in the French Concession. The detectives of the Suzhou-Songjiang Water Bandit Suppression Command arrested the three bandits. They were extradited to Suzhou. After interrogation by the chief of the military law office, the bandits Ding, etc. confessed without hesitation. Except for the bandit Ding Xibiao, whose crime was relatively minor and was sent to the court for trial separately, the two bandits Ding Xitian and Weng Desheng were sentenced to death in accordance with the Regulations on Punishing Bandits. After being submitted to the provincial government for approval, they were executed by firing squad in Suzhou yesterday morning (the 7th).

The Attitude of Foreign Banks Amidst the Calls to Abolish the Taels and Implement the Yuan 125

▲ They Advocate Waiting for Ten or Twenty Years

▲ The Aim is to Preserve Control Over Financial Power

Since the Ministry of Finance expressed its determination to implement the abolition of taels and the adoption of the yuan and established a committee to study the issue, chambers of commerce in various regions and industries in this city have expressed their support. However, they advocate that serious attention must be paid to the fineness of the new currency and the supervisory measures for issuing banknotes thereafter. However, Mr. Mukshot, the representative of foreign banks, has different views on the yuan reform. A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency, considering that the abolition of taels is related to the settlement of foreign trade and telegram prices, specifically investigated the news about this matter as follows:

▲ The Attitude of Foreign Banks Mr. Mukshot, the representative of foreign banks, expressed his attitude to the Research Committee of the Ministry of Finance in writing, advocating that the abolition of taels and the adoption of the yuan should be implemented only after ten or twenty years. The reason is based on the average number of taels over the past ten years being 7 taels, 2 fen, 1 li, 7 hao, and 5 si. Therefore, he believes that the assumed weight of the new silver coin, which is 7 taels and 9 li, is too low. The mint must manufacture coins of the same weight and fineness as those currently circulating in the market. The government should bear the minting cost, which is approximately 1.5 million to 2.5 million yuan per month. The abolition of taels should be implemented after sufficient new silver coins have been prepared. In short, while not opposing it in principle, he actually advocates delaying it.

▲ Rebuttal by Chinese Committee Regarding the statement made by Mr. Mukshot, the representative of foreign banks, Chinese committee members such as Chen Xing and Bei Songsun refuted it at the research committee meeting. They argued that the abolition of taels and the adoption of the yuan is the best opportunity at this time when silver dollars are rampant and foreign exchange rates are plummeting. If we wait for ten or twenty years, market changes may make it impossible to implement. Moreover, if the new silver coins are of better fineness, the government's minting and private remelting will mean that the new coins will never be sufficient for use, and the abolition of taels will never be implemented. As for the cost of minting silver coins, it should be borne by the people, as is the case in Germany, France, and Japan. This is because the current situation of the government makes it impossible to bear this expense.

▲ The Proposal From Ten Years Ago Mr. G.H. Stitt, the manager of the Shanghai branch of the former Hongkong and Shanghai Banking Corporation, delivered a speech on the abolition of taels and the adoption of the yuan at a meeting of the British Chamber of Commerce in Shanghai in 1920. He briefly stated that the foreign chambers of commerce resolved at a meeting in Shanghai in 1919 to request the Chinese government to abolish silver taels and unify the silver subsidiary coins and copper coins of the whole country. They also proposed establishing a mint in Shanghai to freely mint silver coins so as to effectively manage the mint and maintain a single standard system. It is heard that the Chinese government has formally accepted the proposal, and the authorities are inclined to accept it. Two years ago, the foreign banks exchanged views with the financial authorities. The banks mostly acknowledged that the abolition of silver taels and the unification of silver coins would be very beneficial. Although the banking industry currently benefits considerably from the exchange of silver taels and the conversion between taels and yuan, it is believed that the unification of silver coins will have a very good impact on commerce. Although the benefits of silver taels will be lost at that time, the gains will outweigh the losses. However, the unification of silver coins must be extremely strict so that its fineness and weight are consistent throughout the country and the same as the currencies of European and American countries. Then the new system will be able to be promoted without hindrance. From this, it can be seen that the foreign banks at that time also very much hoped that the abolition of taels and the adoption of the yuan could be implemented.

▲ The Key to Advocating Delay The foreign banks already suggested to the Chinese government to abolish taels and adopt the yuan twelve years ago. Now that the government is determined to implement it, they say that it should be waited for ten or twenty years. A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency specifically asked someone who is very familiar with the financial situation yesterday about the reasons for the foreign banks' advocacy of delay. According to the discussion, this abolition of taels and the adoption of the yuan is intended to unify the monetary system internally and recover financial sovereignty externally. Because Shanghai's market now uses silver taels as the unit of account, (1) large-scale imports are currency, and the power over supply and demand is controlled by foreigners. After the abolition of taels, large bars will only be a kind of commodity. If it is to become silver coins, it must go through the central mint for minting. Once silver taels are abolished, the right to valuation will be transferred to the central bank. Due to the above two reasons, foreign banks advocate delay, or they may be affected by the concept of private interests, hoping to retain their control.

After the New Rice From Pudong Came on the Market 134

▲ Rice Prices Fall Gradually

The earliest new rice produced in Shanghai's rice market has always been from Zhoupu and other places in Pudong, and this year's production is even earlier than last year. Since the end of last month, since new rice from Pudong came on the market, the arrival of goods has been booming day by day. The initial opening price was 15 yuan per stone, but sales were sluggish, so the arriving goods could not be sold out immediately. Therefore, the opening price gradually fell. However, it has only been ten days since it came on the market, and yesterday the high-quality goods opened at 13 yuan and 2 jiao, a price drop of more than 1 yuan and 8 jiao compared to before. It is said that the harvest in the Pudong area is still good, and the quality of the goods shipped is also not inferior. Currently, only three or four production areas are harvesting. In the future, as new rice from various places in Pudong is harvested, the source of supply to Shanghai will become even more abundant. Since new rice has come on the market, the sales of japonica rice and foreign rice have been unusually sluggish. Various rice shops, seeing the low price of the new rice, are waiting and watching before buying, so the market price is difficult to improve. However, the supply of high-quality rice is scarce, and the price remains firm. The harvest of rice from Xixin, Suzhou, Songjiang, Changshu, and Wuxi is the largest, and the harvest is later. In previous years, new rice always came on the market at the end of September. According to people in the industry, they recently received letters from the Changshu and Wuxi production areas reporting that the fields have been abnormally arid due to the lack of rain for a long time. Although there is no damage at the moment, if it does not rain again, the fields will definitely be damaged in the future, and the harvest will be difficult to be bountiful.

The Relationship Between the Northern Goods Industry and the Zhuang Ke 136

On June 20th, Nanshi Dingtai, Changtai, Xinchengtai, and Xinbei, northern goods firms, entrusted lawyer Yin Shijie and accountant Pan Xulun to declare liquidation in the newspaper. There were debts owed to Hengxingmao, Hengxingsheng, Dajuchun, Wanchang, and Qianyuan and other firms in Songjiang. The Northern Goods Industry Association's reply to the Jiang County Chamber of Commerce requesting the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce to forward the official letters between the two parties is recorded as follows: (1) Official letter from the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce to the Northern Goods Industry Association, (Excerpted) We received an official letter from the Songjiang County Chamber of Commerce this month, stating that according to a letter from the Songjiang Southern Goods, Tea, and Food Industry Association, "Our members Hengxingmao, Hengxingsheng, Dajuchun, Wanchang, and Qianyuan stated in a letter that our members have always purchased goods from Shanghai through Zhuang Ke Jiang Jinru, and all payments have been cleared on time. However, after the bankruptcy of Shanghai Dingtai, Changtai, Xinchengtai, and Xinbei, three firms, this year, the entrusted lawyer Yin Shijie, in liquidation, suddenly received a letter from lawyer Yin on July 8, claiming that our members owed various amounts of money to Dingtai and other three firms, and immediately prepared a reply denying it. It has been a long-standing practice in our industry to have Zhuang Ke. Inland stores purchase goods through Zhuang Ke. Therefore, the invoices are sent by each firm to the Zhuang Ke for indirect transfer, and the remittances are also handed over to the Zhuang Ke for indirect payment. The existence of Zhuang Ke in our industry is no different from the existence of brokers in the stock exchange. Zhuang Ke's handling of goods is the same as brokers acting as buyers and sellers. Moreover, our members have receipts and invoices for all transactions. However, lawyer Yin repeatedly urges us by letter, and the procedures are wrong. Moreover, a notice is posted in the Shanghai Northern Goods Industry Association, prohibiting the industry from selling various goods to our members. Please provide assistance." Based on this, a temporary meeting was convened on July 26 to discuss the response. After public discussion, it was decided that, based on the above circumstances, a letter should be sent to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, instructing the Shanghai Northern Goods Industry Association to withdraw the notice posted by Hengxingmao and other associations in order to protect their reputation, etc., recorded in the minutes. Accordingly, a letter is sent for your information and implementation. The details are as follows. Please reply clearly so that we can forward the letter. (2) The Northern Goods Industry's reply to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, In reply, we received a letter containing (Excerpted) etc. Article 2 of our industry rules states that when customers patronize transactions, they should register the invoice number and pay the money. Article 3 states that inland customers and Zhuang Ke are originally partners and should communicate with each other without any gaps. If the customer is in trouble, the Zhuang Ke should be responsible for compensation. If the Zhuang Ke is in debt, the amount owed should be collected from the inland customer. If they shirk responsibility, they should gather at the industry association meeting to deal with it. The nature of the Shanghai Zhuang Ke is that they are the purchasers entrusted by the inland merchants, in other words, they are the employees of the inland merchants. Therefore, usually, inland merchants purchase goods from our industry through the Shanghai Zhuang Ke, and the invoices are registered with the brand names of the inland stores. The receipt of money is based on the receipts of the firms. It has been followed for decades without any difference. Moreover, this practice is not only the case in our industry, but also in other industries such as the sugar industry, seafood industry, miscellaneous goods industry, and longan industry. Their rules are roughly the same. Now, the statements made by Hengxingmao, Juxingsheng, Dajuchun, Wanchang, Qianyuan, and others are completely contrary to the facts and without sufficient reason. The fact that the Zhuang Ke collected money from these firms is that the Zhuang Ke collected it privately. It is actually the inland merchants who are negligent in using their own personnel. It is already a very serious negligence. Now they do not blame themselves but instead blame others. This is the first contradiction. It is also claimed that they have receipts as evidence. The so-called receipts are the receipts of the Zhuang Ke, not the receipts of the firms. If they were indeed receipts from the firms, how could there be a reason to claim the debt again? This is the second contradiction. It is also claimed that the existence of Zhuang Ke in our industry is no different from the brokers in the stock exchange. This is an even more far-fetched analogy. It is important to know that in the stock exchange, both the buyer and the seller recognize the broker as the basis, and only the margin is the goal of short selling and long buying. They do not ask who the buyer is or who the seller is. Our industry and other industries such as the sugar industry, seafood industry, miscellaneous goods industry, and longan industry are purely formal transactions and not speculative in nature. Therefore, they all trust the brand names of the inland stores as the main body, and the Zhuang Ke is completely the manager of the inland merchants. Why do Hengxingmao and others try to shirk responsibility and not understand the truth to this extent? This is the third contradiction. The posting of a notice is a natural measure for our industry to fulfill its duties and deal with the matter in accordance with the rules. Based on the above rules and practices, our industry Dingtai, etc., has not violated anything. We should give a detailed reply and hope that you will carefully examine it, approve the forwarding of the letter to the Songjiang County Chamber of Commerce, and ask the Chamber of Commerce to consult the Songjiang Southern Goods, Tea, and Food Industry Association and forward it to Hengxingmao, Hengxingsheng, Dajuchun, Wanchang, and Qianyuan, etc., to quickly clear the debts owed to Dingtai, Changtai, Xinchengtai, and Xinbei three firms, and to transfer the debts to facilitate the closing. We sincerely request your friendship. It is also heard that the Northern Goods Industry Association believes that this debt dispute is of great importance to the overall commercial debt of Shanghai and will jointly hold a joint meeting with the sugar industry, seafood industry, and miscellaneous goods industry to discuss appropriate countermeasures in order to emphasize debt and publicize justice.

Mu Chia-chi Studies Advanced Academic Pursuits 139

Mr. Mu Chia-chi, a native of Shanghai, Jiangsu, is 26 years old and the second son of the renowned industrialist Mr. Mu Ouchu. With a deep family academic background, he is highly proficient in both Chinese and English. After graduating from the High School Affiliated to Jiaotong University in Shanghai, he went to the United States to study. [Image of Mr. Mu Chia-chi]

He achieved excellent results and was highly regarded by his teachers. Mr. Mu is not content with this achievement and will be entering the graduate school of Columbia University this autumn to pursue advanced academic studies. He is expected to obtain a doctoral degree next summer. At that time, he plans to travel to Europe for observation before returning to China to apply his knowledge and serve his country. Our political and economic circles will gain another talented individual.

Bomb Explodes in a Garden in Dachang, Injuring Two Gardeners 140

▲ A Calamity Left Behind by Japanese Soldiers

Around 12 o'clock the night before last, in the Yongli Farm, about two li north of Dachang Town, which is along the Shanghai-Taicang long-distance bus route, several gardeners were enjoying the cool air in the garden. Due to the excessive number of mosquitoes, they burned mosquito repellent. Unexpectedly, a bomb left behind by Japanese soldiers was buried in the soil under a pile of garbage. It exploded due to the heat, producing a loud noise. Two gardeners were injured by the explosion, with blood and flesh flying everywhere, a tragic sight to behold. It is reported that the injured have been sent to Huaisheng Hospital for treatment.

Letter Carrier Convicted of Stealing Stamps 141

▲ Sentenced to Six Months in Prison

Wu Baoqing, a Ningbo native working as a letter carrier at the North Sichuan Road Post Office, secretly opened letters and stole stamps between March and August of this year. This was reported to the office's investigators. At around 5 p.m. the day before yesterday, Tao and Ge, two investigators, saw Wu examining letters by hand, trying to feel if there were stamps inside. They questioned him, but he gave evasive answers. They also saw that a letter had been torn open and discarded on the table. They picked up the letter as evidence and telegraphed the Hongkou Police Station. The detective Yang Xichen arrived and arrested Wu, also searching his home at No. 32, New Jiaqiao Road, Zhabei, and finding dozens of new and used stamps worth fourteen dollars, which were brought to the police station. The next morning, he was sent to the Fourth Criminal Division of the First Special District Court. The police lawyer Zhang Tianyin presented the facts of the case, submitted the stamps and the torn letter as evidence, and requested a severe investigation to prevent others from following suit. Subsequently, investigators Tao and Ge presented a report detailing the circumstances. Questioned, the defendant claimed that the stamps were purchased with his own money and intended to be taken back to his hometown. He claimed that some of them were found on the floor in the post office and denied tearing open the letter, claiming it had gaps when it arrived. His answers were evasive. After verification by Judge Fu Lin, Wu Baoqing was sentenced on the spot for repeatedly opening letters to serve as a warning. The police lawyer Zhang requested that the recovered stamps be returned to the plaintiff, which the court approved.

Apprentice Falls to Death from Drying Platform 142

Lu Juhai, a 17-year-old from Tongzhou, was an apprentice at the carpentry shop of Ling Youqiao at No. 188 Tianjin Road. Around 1 p.m. on the 14th of last month, he went to the drying platform to hang clothes but accidentally slipped and fell, injuring his head and other areas. The shop owner, Ling Youqiao, saw him and sent him to Renji Hospital for treatment. However, he died from his injuries the day before yesterday. The body was sent to the forensic examination office on Faelun Road. Yesterday morning, Guo, the prosecutor appointed by the First Special District Court, along with forensic doctor Zhang Yan and clerk Wang Zuyi, arrived at the office to examine the body. Ling Youqiao testified that the deceased had washed his own clothes that day and went to the drying platform alone, so no one saw how he fell. He only knew after he fell to the ground when he heard a loud noise. The deceased's mother, Lu Yuan, also provided a statement. Guo then concluded that Lu Juhai died from injuries sustained from a fall. The body was handed over to Lu Yuan after she signed a guarantee to take it back for burial.

Another Person Involved in French Newspaper Robbery Case Apprehended 143

▲ To Be Tried Together

The French newspaper office on Avenue Edward VII was robbed at noon on the 30th of last month, when thieves broke into the accounting office on the second floor and stole over two thousand yuan in payroll cash before escaping. Zhuang Huanwen and Xu Ruiyuan (the French newspaper's assistant accountant), who were implicated in the case, have been apprehended by the police. One hundred yuan was found on Xu. They were sent to court for interrogation and investigation. Recently, the Chinese and Western detectives handling the case apprehended another person involved, Yao Amao, who was sent to the First Criminal Division of the Second Special District Court the day before yesterday. The police lawyer Gu Shouxi stated that the defendants Zhuang and Xu had already been apprehended and were under investigation. Now that another defendant has been apprehended, he requested a postponement for a joint trial. Presiding Judge Wang Gangxu questioned the defendant briefly and then approved the postponement of the trial to the 23rd of this month. The defendant was taken into custody.

Robbers Shoot Zhang Dingsheng 144

Zhang Dingsheng, a 26-year-old Ningbo native, runs the Huaxiang Department Store at No. 957, Qingyuli, Dong Hanbi Road, Hongkou. His wife, Wang, is also from Ningbo. At approximately 10:15 p.m. last night, she went out to get water, leaving only Dingsheng in the store. Suddenly, two men in blue cotton shirts and pants entered. Zhang, thinking they were customers, greeted them. Unexpectedly, the two men pulled out pistols and told him not to make a sound. They then entered the store and robbed some silver coins and other items from the cash register. As they were about to flee, Dingsheng, known for his loud voice, shouted "Robbers!" Fearing that the police would arrive, one of the robbers fired three shots, hitting Zhang in his left palm, right chest, and lower abdomen. He collapsed to the ground. Seeing the trouble they had caused, the robbers fled. Zhang's wife, Wang, returned with the water and saw him lying in a pool of blood, unconscious. The neighbors gathered, and they hired a car to send him to Tongren Hospital for treatment. It is said that his life is in danger. They also reported the incident to the Hongkou Police Station, who sent detectives to investigate and track down the robbers.

Mayor Wu Praises the Products of the Mayer Silk Weaving Factory 146

The Shanghai Mayer Silk Weaving Factory has been established for twelve years, entirely with Chinese capital, operated by Chinese people, and employing Chinese workers. It uses domestic silk to manufacture domestic silk fabrics, producing more than 300,000 pieces annually, which are sold throughout the world. It also has its own dyeing, refining, and printing factories, introducing new and colorful designs. In June of this year, it specially sent assistant manager Mr. Gao Shiheng and more than ten employees to bring hundreds of new products to South China, including Hong Kong, Guangzhou, Chaozhou, Xiamen, Shantou, Fuzhou, Quanzhou, Wenzhou, Ningbo, to hold product promotion exhibitions, advocating the use of domestic silk fabrics. In all the cities they visited, they were joined by local party, government, military, business, academic circles, and prominent women, who gave speeches praising the products. The scale of the events surpassed that of previous domestic goods exhibitions in South China. Recently, the factory's products were praised by Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng as the "King of National Goods," and the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce and other public organizations certified that the silk fabrics were woven from domestic silk. As a result, people have been eagerly purchasing the factory's seasonal fabrics. To prevent the mixing of inferior goods, the factory has specially woven its factory name and Mayer trademark on all its products as a mark.

Recently, due to the high price of gold and low price of silver, the exchange rate between silver dollars and copper coins has also risen sharply. Yesterday, the market rate for silver was 430,500 wen per hundred taels, equivalent to 2,961 wen per silver dollar, or 5 jiao 8 fen 3 li. One silver dollar could be exchanged for 452 wen per ten-cent coin, or 6 jiao 8 fen 8 li. One tael of pure gold could be exchanged for 111.5 silver dollars.

Dispute Over Valuables Involving Jin Cuiyu 148

▲ Mr. Zhang Dies with Unclosed Eyes

Jin Cuiyu, a Shanghai Ningbo Opera actress, aged 24, fell in love with Mr. Zhang, who was in the electrical business, five years ago and lived together in a rented house for five years. Later, they broke up halfway and separated a few months ago. Recently, Mr. Zhang suddenly died of a serious illness. Jin rushed to the scene before Zhang's body was even in a coffin, arguing over the furniture in the room. The details of this incident are as follows:

▲ Extravagant Lifestyle: Mr. Zhang was in the electrical business and had a good monthly income. In addition to renting a house for his wife in Guian Lane in the French Concession, he cohabitated with Jin Cuiyu, a Ningbo Opera actress, five years ago. Initially, they rented a house on Zhejiang Road in the International Settlement and purchased furniture, silk mosquito nets, and other supplies, spending a total of 40,000 to 50,000 yuan over the years.

▲ Empty Room: In the early summer of this year, Zhang was sued in the International Settlement, and Jin took advantage of this to break up with Zhang, planning to go to Hankou to join an opera troupe and leave Shanghai. (Actually, she only left Zhang but not Shanghai). She rented a house elsewhere. As a result, the house rented by Zhang was left empty for several months. Last month, Zhang's lawsuit was resolved, and he moved the furniture from this room to the upstairs of a certain parlor in Renmei Lane in the French Concession. The arrangement of the room remained the same, and Zhang even hung Jin's photo in the room, hoping that Jin would return soon.

▲ Arriving During the Funeral: Recently, due to the hot weather and the prevalence of epidemics, Zhang suddenly died of a serious illness in his residence in Guian Lane a few days ago. While relatives and friends were gathering to discuss funeral arrangements, Jin Cuiyu received the news and rushed to the scene. She wanted to argue over the furniture and boxes in the room in Renmei Lane, claiming that they were purchased with her own money and did not belong to Zhang. After repeated discussions, it was decided that Jin Cuiyu would pay a certain amount of funeral expenses before she was allowed to take away the furniture.

For mail orders from other cities, postage is free.
