Letter to the Editor 165

To the Editor-in-Chief of Shen Bao,

Respectfully, upon reading the article "Boatmen and Police Officers Fight" in the news column of your newspaper on the 5th of this month, it is inconsistent with the facts. It was found that at around 6 p.m. on the 3rd of this month, two stone boats loaded with stones from the Tangkou Bureau were moored at the black floating point outside Wusongkou. Due to the wind and tide, they could not reach their destination for unloading, so the boatmen were playing mahjong on the boat for recreation. Suddenly, two armed water police officers came to the boat to arrest them. The boatmen panicked and fled, which angered the water police officers, who threatened them with guns. One of the boatmen fell into the water and has not been found since. Seeing this situation, the boatmen argued with the water police officers, and it was alleged that the water police officers lost a wooden-cased gun with a Kowloon belt. Seeing that it had resulted in a death and that they had lost their weapons, the water police officers returned to the team on the grounds that the boatmen were resisting arrest and sent more water police officers to the boat for a second time. They arrested all the boatmen on both ships (except for one who fell into the water and one child who was watching the boat), totaling nine people. The families of the arrested boatmen have entrusted this lawyer with legal relief. The news previously published in your newspaper is inconsistent with the facts, and I am afraid that it will cause misunderstandings from the outside world. Therefore, I have prepared this letter requesting your newspaper to correct it in the letter column in order to clarify the truth and show the facts. I wish you good health.

Lawyer Jiang Gongjian, August 7th

Guo Luo Commits Suicide 166

— Buddha

Yesterday's newspapers reported two more suicide cases. One was Guo Mingxing, nephew of Guo Songling, who committed suicide in Hangzhou due to excessive stimulation. The other was Luo Yancun, a student at Qingdao University, who committed suicide because he felt unjustly expelled from school. I believe that neither of these cases warranted suicide. This is a sign of the weak will and lack of deep, strong character among young people today. Because to be a person, one must fight one's way out of hardship and difficulty; that is the true path to survival. A career built from overcoming obstacles is a true career. If one resorts to suicide after a single failure or setback, that mentality is completely wrong.

(1) Guo Mingxing, nephew of Guo Songling, whose entire family was brutally murdered, even if he had personally avenged them, it would not have been enough to vent his irreconcilable hatred. Therefore, he wanted to sneak into the border region of Heilongjiang Province to gather his father's old troops and resist the Japanese army. This was such a great ambition that it is truly admirable. Unexpectedly, due to the exhaustion of travel funds, he suddenly had suicidal thoughts, which was a great mistake. To seek revenge, one must preserve one's own existence, so that revenge can be achieved. If one destroys oneself first, it is equivalent to not wanting to take revenge and being avenged by the enemy first. This is one reason why he should not have died. Moreover, people are afraid of sacrifice, but if they are willing to sacrifice, they should obtain a corresponding price. Even if Guo could not gather his father's old troops to resist the Japanese army, even individual sacrifice could still obtain a corresponding price, then his sacrifice would have value. In the past, Wu Zixu was willing to play the flute in the market of Wu to avenge the murder of his father, and Shen Baoxu cried for seven days and seven nights in the Qin court to restore the state of Wu, and finally avenged the state of Wu. What a fierce, meaningful, and valuable revenge!

(2) Luo Zicun, because his family was poor and unable to afford schooling, received assistance from the provincial government and relatives to enter Qingdao University. However, due to student unrest at Qingdao University, Luo was expelled, and he felt he had no face to return home, so he committed suicide passively. I have two opinions to explain this. First, the school authorities expelled Luo, but Luo asked himself if he had violated school rules or failed any exams. This was an error on the part of the school authorities, and Luo only needed to have a clear conscience. It can be said that it had nothing to do with Luo. Second, if expulsion means a damaged reputation and no chance to transfer, I have a suggestion. I ask, can a university diploma be pawned nowadays? Can it be exchanged for food? On the one hand, there are more and more university graduates, and on the other hand, many university graduates are illiterate and unable to translate an English article. There are many such people. One studies because one wants to learn, not because of a diploma. Therefore, the ninety-three-year-old Ma Xiangbo once said that graduating from middle school is like getting a key to a bookcase. If you want to study any subject, you just need to find it yourself. So, it is not necessarily the case that a university graduate is knowledgeable, and a non-university graduate is ignorant. Originally, universities are now aristocratic; only the children of a few capitalists have the privilege of studying there. Poor children can only crane their necks and look in from the outside. (I have vowed that when I study in the future, I plan to organize a large-scale academic society where all poor children can join and freely discuss and study with each other, but there is no concrete plan yet.) Look at the famous scholars of ancient times, who initially were herdsmen or slaves, or studied by the light of snow or fireflies, or pricked their thighs with awls, and eventually became the masters of their generation. There are countless such examples. Why must one go to an aristocratic university to study now?

Therefore, regarding the issue of studying, I have no hope of helping the country or society in any way. Young people should find their own solutions and ways out, especially poor students. They should study hard and diligently on their own. Universities cannot be relied on, teachers cannot be relied on, and money cannot be relied on. Only your own great and intelligent brain is the most reliable. If you spend two or three thousand dollars to buy a worthless diploma, what is the use? What is its value?

Literature and Art

Occasional Thoughts While Strolling in the Bund Park 167

— Mo Hongshan

A wandering traveler, living in Shanghai, with few social interactions and friends, feeling bored on a summer day, with the scorching sun setting, I strolled through the Bund Park and was moved to write: The Yangtze River flows leisurely, the trees on the Bund are lush, the sun sets and the birds want to roost, seen far in the depths of the forest. White cicadas bloom in order, green reeds brush the water obliquely, the vegetation is full of human intention, quiet and beautiful.

Standing by the embankment, the sea breeze takes advantage of the cool evening, brushing past shoulders. Who passed by? A faint fragrance of night-blooming jasmine is heard. Disordered masts dot the night like stars, shining faintly beyond the Bund. Borrowing the mood of the Pearl River, it must be lacking songs and music.

Science

Machine Oil 168

— Zuo

Machine oil (lubricant) is the common name for lubricating material. Most people do not pay much attention to it, but they do not know that it has made a great contribution to modern civilization. Without it, the countless shafts that provide clothing, food, supplies, and knowledge would come to a halt; all machines, from small watches to the turbines of power plants, would stop working; factories and transportation equipment would stagnate, and the source of food and other necessities would be cut off. The modern mechanical world was created by the invention of the axle, but the invention of machine oil helped to achieve this.

What is the function of machine oil? Before answering this question, we must first know what friction is. Try placing a very smooth surface under a microscope, and you will see countless thorns, like a cat's tongue. When two surfaces are pressed together and moved, these thorns hook into each other and impede movement. This impediment is called friction. The amount of friction depends entirely on the roughness of the surface and the amount of force applied.

The purpose of applying machine oil is to separate the two surfaces so that they do not pull on each other and can move freely. According to precise research, the oil film applied between the two surfaces is divided into at least three layers: the upper and lower layers are tightly attached to each surface and move with it, while the middle layer or layers are suspended in the middle. Therefore, what slides over each other is actually liquid, not solid. This is how machine oil lubricates machine parts and makes them move freely.

The thickness of the oil film between the two surfaces has no bearing on the lubrication effect. Someone once used A-rays to test that a thin layer of oil film only a few molecules thick applied to a car engine achieved an exceptionally satisfactory lubrication effect. All axles in the world are spinning rapidly on this magical oil film. When the axle is stationary, it touches the bottom of the bearing, squeezing the oil to the sides. But when the axle rotates, it draws the oil to the bottom, and the axle floats in the air, with the oil film as the bottom cushion. An experimenter once used precision instruments to measure that the axle rises about two to three thousandths of an inch when rotating.

Improving Society

The Prerequisite for Abolishing Superstition: How to Eliminate Superstition 169

— Cheng Hao

Yesterday, Ms. Ouyang published an article in this journal on abolishing superstition, advocating that the money wasted on praying to gods and worshipping Buddha should be used for undertakings beneficial to society and the country. I strongly agree with this view. However, I believe that it will be very difficult to achieve this goal unless the superstitious beliefs of the general public are first removed. Therefore, there is a prerequisite: how to eliminate superstition?

The meaning of (superstition) is to believe in something while confused and without awareness. Because it is a kind of confused and unaware belief, it is deeply ingrained in the mind and very difficult to break. The superstitious belief in ghosts and gods among the general public in our country has been subtly instilled since childhood and deeply imprinted in their minds, making it difficult to eradicate. Although there has been a slogan of "overthrowing superstition" circulating in society in recent years, the potential power of superstition is still very strong, and most people are still heavily intoxicated by demons and unaware of themselves. We only need to go to the Hongmiao Temple and the City God Temple to see that every day, many men, women, old and young, are very enthusiastically and solemnly burning incense, lighting candles, chanting, and worshipping Buddha. Shanghai is a very modern place, yet it is still like this. The situation in other provinces and counties can naturally be imagined. Moreover, most superstitious people are very stubborn and unreasonable. If you tell them that praying to gods and worshipping Buddha cannot bring blessings or ward off disasters and is a futile act, no one will pay attention to you. No matter how sufficient your reasons are or how clearly you explain, they will never be convinced. Because they have been held captive by the evil demon and are difficult to free. The author has repeatedly promoted the elimination of superstition at home but has been severely criticized, and family relationships have almost been broken as a result. The difficulty of eradicating superstition can be seen from this. Therefore, I believe that the (superstition) problem is really a very important social problem in our country and also the most difficult problem to solve.

A True Story from an Examination 170

— Hou Ying

Inside XX Middle School, many new students were taking exams in history, geography, and nature.

"Hey! Hey, excuse me, is Tianjin in Shandong Province?"

A short, stocky friend asked a slightly taller friend sitting next to him. The slightly taller friend first looked up at the proctor, then gently said to him, "Yes." But on his own test paper, he wrote the three characters "Hebei Province" in pencil.

The three major river basins of China? (1) Yangtze River, (2) Yellow River, (3) ... Oh: the Yangtze River!"

The short friend put down his pen, held his head in both hands, and just kept thinking.

"That's right, it must be the Yangtze River!"

The short friend said to himself again, then picked up his pen and wrote in what he thought was the correct (three major river basins of China).

Half an hour later, the slightly taller friend had finished all ten questions. He stood up to hand in his paper. When he came back, he saw the short friend's answer to the third question:

(China was unified by foreign ethnic groups twice), (Answer: Tang and Song.)

The slightly taller friend could not help but sneer. Later, he learned that he was the son of an XX teacher, and his name was XX.

Several days later, the list of new students admitted to XX Middle School was announced. The taller friend also took a newspaper and looked at it, but no matter how he looked, he could not find his name, but only the three characters XX were prominently displayed before his eyes!
